> Pensado para 1m 35s

**Logline Lab Definition And Primitives**

# LogLine Lab — Definition, Scope, Primitives, and Evidence Discipline

**Status:** founding definition / canon candidate  
**Layer:** LogLine Lab public kit and practice primitive  
**Purpose:** freeze what a LogLine Lab is before implementation, scale, branding, or local deployment obscure the concept  
**Parent:** LogLine Foundation, unchanged  
**Children:** local labs, Santo André Laboratory, Dan/minilab.work overlay, community labs, domain-specific labs  
**Motto:** We Trust and Build with LogLine.

---

## 0. Founding Sentence

A **LogLine Lab** is a living laboratory kit for studying LogLine itself and building with LogLine under real conditions.

It gives people a way to load the LogLine canon, declare local practice, register runtimes, emit acts, run probes, project worlds, preserve ghosts, prepare receipts, and study what happens when LogLine moves through software, AI, contracts, simulations, databases, agents, people, and reality.

A LogLine Lab does not prescribe scale, budget, programming language, cloud provider, or research agenda.

It provides primitives.

Each lab adds infrastructure according to its own resources, risks, interests, jurisdiction, and ambition.

---

## 1. Public Position

```txt
LogLine Foundation is the grammar.
LogLine Lab is the practice kit.
A local lab is a declared instantiation.
```

A LogLine Lab is not the Foundation.

A LogLine Lab is not a product category.

A LogLine Lab is not a dashboard.

A LogLine Lab is not an AI agent framework.

A LogLine Lab is not a database schema.

A LogLine Lab is not a single runtime.

A LogLine Lab is not Dan's private infrastructure.

A LogLine Lab is a kit for creating a place where LogLine can be studied, run, projected, tested, doubted, and built with.

---

## 2. Non-Amendment Rule

A LogLine Lab does not silently change LogLine canon.

If the Lab introduces operational discipline not present in LogLine Foundation, it must declare that discipline as Lab practice, local practice, or experimental practice.

Allowed:

```txt
This lab requires runtime envelopes.
This lab projects passports from register_entity acts.
This lab projects visas from issue_visa acts.
This lab uses Supabase as projection substrate.
This lab runs a 24/7 AI clock.
This lab studies interval semantics.
```

Forbidden:

```txt
Claiming local lab rules are Foundation canon.
Hiding operational assumptions inside infrastructure.
Treating a database projection as parent truth.
Treating a runtime convention as universal LogLine law.
```

A LogLine Lab may produce discoveries that later become upstream proposals.

Until accepted upstream, they remain Lab practice or local overlay.

---

## 3. What a LogLine Lab Studies

A LogLine Lab studies **LogLine itself in motion**.

It studies:

```txt
acts
engines
runtimes
runtime envelopes
content-addressed identity
composition
projections
receipts
ghosts
probes
intervals
simulations
real runs
contracts
AI translation into acts
self-parsing
self-bootstrap
what runs natively above software
```

It may also use LogLine to study other domains, but that is secondary.

Primary research object:

```txt
LogLine as a compact act grammar moving through engines, runtimes, projections, procedures, humans, AI, and reality.
```

---

## 4. What a LogLine Lab Does

A LogLine Lab performs six basic functions.

### 4.1 Load

It loads LogLine canon and any declared practice profiles.

```txt
load canon
load conformance
load engine
load local practice
load runtime registry
load projectors
```

### 4.2 Declare

It declares its local practice.

```txt
lab name
purpose
jurisdiction
clock discipline
runtimes
projectors
ghost policy
receipt policy
proof policy
evidence policy
```

### 4.3 Observe

It observes language, systems, models, contracts, computations, simulations, and human decisions as potential LogLine material.

Observation does not equal proof.

Observation becomes proof only when admitted, referenced, and projected through an appropriate evidence path.

### 4.4 Emit

It emits LogLine Acts and candidate acts.

Acts may represent:

```txt
claims
questions
probes
runtime results
decisions
bindings
permissions
contracts
experiments
receipts
ghosts
state changes
reports
```

### 4.5 Project

It projects acts into useful read models.

Examples:

```txt
registry
runtimes
visas
passports
evidence
receipts
ghosts
experiments
audit views
reports
standards adapters
```

Projection gives domain meaning.

Projection is not semantic source.

### 4.6 Learn

It studies what happened.

Learning may produce:

```txt
new probes
new projectors
new runtimes
new ghosts
new receipts
new local rules
new upstream proposals
new failures worth preserving
```

---

## 5. What a LogLine Lab Does Not Do

A LogLine Lab does not prescribe:

```txt
scale
budget
cloud provider
programming language
database engine
AI model vendor
hardware profile
research topic
business domain
social form
public/private posture
```

A LogLine Lab does not require a corporation, foundation, university, lab building, GPU cluster, or formal institution.

A LogLine Lab may be:

```txt
a personal lab
a research lab
a company lab
a civic lab
a classroom lab
a contract lab
a simulation lab
a local AI lab
a governance lab
a software lab
a physical machine lab
a public-interest lab
```

The Lab gives primitives.

The operator chooses scale.

---

## 6. Core Primitive: LogLine Act

Every semantic movement in a LogLine Lab should be representable as a LogLine Act.

Canonical semantic shape:

```txt
who
did
this
when
confirmed_by
if_ok
if_doubt
if_not
status
```

The nine slots are the compact backbone.

They preserve:

```txt
agent
action
object/material/claim
time
confirmation path
success route
doubt route
failure route
epistemic or operational state
```

A LogLine Lab may use additional envelopes, projections, indexes, tables, files, reports, and artifacts.

These do not replace the act.

---

## 7. Static Atom, Dynamic Translation

LogLine is small and static.

Current LLMs make it newly practical because they can translate natural language into the nine-slot act grammar with low semantic loss.

The translation is not lossless.

It has loss comparable to translation between natural languages, not the severe loss of forcing living intention into a static paper form by hand.

LogLine does not eliminate ambiguity.

It gives ambiguity a route:

```txt
if_doubt
```

What cannot honestly be frozen as certainty is preserved as doubt, probe, ghost, or unresolved state.

---

## 8. Core Primitive: Runtime Envelope

A LogLine Lab may require every admitted or observed act to carry a runtime envelope.

The envelope is not a tenth semantic slot.

The envelope is provenance.

Minimum conceptual envelope:

```yaml
runtime_id:
engine_id:
run_id:
admission_status:
emitted_at:
observed_at:
tuple_hash:
content_hash:
previous_act_refs: []
```

Rule:

```txt
The act is content.
The envelope is provenance.
```

The act says what happened.

The envelope says where, how, by which runtime, and under which admission/observation path the act entered the Lab.

---

## 9. Core Primitive: Runtime Registry

A LogLine Lab should maintain a projected runtime registry.

The runtime registry describes what a runtime is, what it can emit, what it can admit, what it can observe, and what kinds of acts/projections it is associated with.

Conceptual fields:

```yaml
runtime_id:
runtime_entity_ref:
engine_entity_ref:
lab_id:
status:
capabilities: []
accepted_dids: []
projection_hints: {}
evidence_policy: {}
authority_policy: {}
last_seen_at:
passport_act_ref:
latest_act_ref:
```

Rule:

```txt
The runtime registry is capability.
```

Domain meaning is interpreted through:

```txt
did + this + runtime_id + runtime registry + projector rules
```

---

## 10. Core Primitive: Projection

The semantic database is LogLine.

Tables, views, APIs, dashboards, reports, adapters, indexes, and standard mappings are projections.

```txt
The database is LogLine.
The tables are projections.
```

A projection may be:

```txt
local
private
public
domain-specific
query-optimized
UI-oriented
standard-compatible
compliance-oriented
experimental
disposable
rebuildable
```

A projection may map LogLine Acts into world-known standards when useful.

Examples:

```txt
W3C PROV
OpenTelemetry
RO-Crate
FHIR
GS1 / EPCIS
ActivityPub
OpenAPI / JSON Schema
accounting ledgers
inventory systems
custom domain schemas
```

LogLine does not need to replace world standards.

LogLine can wrap them.

Rule:

```txt
LogLine is the write model.
Standards are projection models.
```

---

## 11. Core Primitive: Ghost

A ghost is preserved absence.

A ghost records what cannot yet be honestly proven, closed, executed, admitted, projected, or decided.

A ghost is not failure.

A ghost is the Lab refusing to lie.

Ghosts may represent missing:

```txt
evidence
runtime
source
signature
permission
receipt path
projection rule
input
witness
reproducibility
conformance
implementation
semantic clarity
```

A ghost should name:

```txt
what is missing
why it matters
what it blocks
who/what owns the next act
what would close or narrow it
```

---

## 12. Core Primitive: Probe

A probe is a bounded attempt to touch reality, computation, or evidence.

A probe may be manual, runtime-driven, AI-assisted, simulated, computational, physical, contractual, or social.

A probe must preserve:

```txt
claim under test
method
runtime or actor
inputs
expected observation
evidence path
doubt path
failure path
```

A probe does not guarantee closure.

A probe produces observation, evidence, ghost, or next probe.

---

## 13. Core Primitive: Evidence

Evidence is a referenceable observation that supports or weakens a claim.

Evidence may come from:

```txt
runtime output
artifact hash
sensor observation
manual witness
signed document
model output under declared limits
simulation result
conformance test
external standard report
transaction trace
contract performance record
```

Evidence is not automatically receipt.

Evidence supports closure only within declared scope.

Evidence should preserve:

```txt
source
runtime or witness
observed_at
artifact refs
hashes when possible
redaction status
scope
limits
```

---

## 14. Core Primitive: Receipt

A receipt is scoped closure projected from admitted acts and evidence.

A receipt is not a native magical object.

It is a LogLine-shaped closure accepted by a receipt projector or review process.

A receipt should say:

```txt
what claim or interval it closes
what evidence supports it
what scope is closed
what scope is not closed
what ghosts remain
what runtime or reviewer admitted closure
```

Forbidden receipt behavior:

```txt
closing broad claims from narrow evidence
calling runtime success proof of system success
calling model output evidence by itself
claiming future guarantee from past observation
hiding ghosts
```

---

## 15. Core Primitive: Passport

A passport is a projection of an admitted identity act.

Typical source act:

```txt
did = register_entity
```

A passport may represent:

```txt
human
agent
LLM office
computer
LAB
engine
runtime
service
OAuth client
MCP tool
app
artifact
jurisdiction
institution
```

The institutional identity anchor is content-addressed.

```txt
passport_ref = act://sha256:<register_entity_act_hash>
```

A table row may store the projection.

The act is the identity source.

---

## 16. Core Primitive: Visa

A visa is a projection of an admitted permission act composed over a passport.

Typical source act:

```txt
did = issue_visa
```

A visa declares:

```txt
subject passport
issuer
capabilities
scope
constraints
audience
expiry
revocation or supersession path
```

A visa is not execution.

A visa is permission.

Execution still requires a relevant process, runtime, workorder, envelope, and evidence path.

---

## 17. Core Primitive: Workorder

A workorder is a projected execution unit.

It is not free language.

It is not authority by itself.

It is a bounded act or act-derived packet that tells a registered runtime what may be attempted under declared scope.

A workorder should define:

```txt
objective
target runtime or LAB
mode
allowed actions
forbidden actions
inputs
expected outputs
evidence requirements
secret policy
rollback or rectify path
receipt path
```

A LogLine Lab may use Hermes or any other runtime to execute workorders.

The runtime is replaceable.

The act discipline is not.

---

## 18. Core Primitive: Clock

A LogLine Lab becomes alive when it has a clock.

The clock gives rhythm to observation, routing, probing, reporting, ghost review, and state projection.

A clock may be manual, scheduled, worker-driven, AI-assisted, or fully automated.

A clock may:

```txt
emit tick acts
check stale ghosts
review runtime heartbeat
prepare state reports
suggest probes
queue dispatch candidates
prepare receipts for review
produce daily and weekly reports
```

A clock may not:

```txt
authorize protected action silently
erase ghosts
close receipts without evidence
mutate external systems without admitted workorders
publish without authority
pretend motion is truth
```

Rule:

```txt
A Lab without a clock is a folder with ambition.
```

---

## 19. Core Primitive: Interval

A LogLine interval is a bounded act field between two boundary acts.

```txt
start boundary act
finish boundary act
```

Inside the interval may exist:

```txt
candidate acts
simulation paths
real runtime runs
observations
evidence
ghosts
receipts
projections
reports
next acts
```

A simulation is a possible path through an interval.

A real run is a path emitted or observed by a registered runtime with envelope provenance.

A result act is not an ending.

It may become input to a future interval.

---

## 20. Core Primitive: Composition

LogLine composition is not Lego-like mechanical symmetry.

It is closer to polar chemistry.

Every act has the same backbone, but different polarity.

```txt
nine slots = common backbone
did + this = side chain
confirmed_by = evidence binding
runtime envelope = environment
prior refs = composition history
projection = observed function
```

Acts bind differently depending on role.

Examples:

```txt
passport acts bind to visa acts
visa acts bind to workorder acts
workorder acts bind to runtime result acts
runtime result acts bind to evidence projections
evidence acts bind to receipt acts
ghost acts bind to next probe acts
```

Composition is directional, contextual, and history-bearing.

---

## 21. Reproducibility

In LogLine, reproducibility is not merely rerunning code.

Reproducibility means the ability to recover and continue the same act-shaped history:

```txt
intention
runtime
evidence
projection
closure
doubt
next experiment
```

Reproducibility includes:

```txt
content reproducibility
provenance reproducibility
projection reproducibility
runtime reproducibility when possible
meaning reproducibility
scientific reproducibility
```

Formula:

```txt
reproducibility =
  content addressability
+ runtime provenance
+ referenced inputs
+ deterministic projection
+ explicit doubt paths
+ composable next acts
```

If full runtime reproducibility is impossible, the Lab preserves the original observation and names the missing reproducibility as a ghost.

---

## 22. Self-Parsing and Self-Bootstrap

LogLine can become self-parsing and self-bootstrapping because its procedure remains inside the grammar.

The consequence slots:

```txt
if_ok
if_doubt
if_not
```

allow acts to route next acts.

A procedure can be represented as a sequence or graph of LogLine Acts.

The system can use LogLine Acts to:

```txt
register its own runtime
declare its own projector
issue its own visa
open its own probe
record its own evidence
carry its own ghost
emit its own receipt
```

It does not bootstrap from nothing.

It bootstraps from a seed:

```txt
nine-slot grammar
engine
hash/admission rule
runtime envelope practice if required
```

After that, the act graph can describe the machine that reads the act graph.

---

## 23. Above Software Thesis

When software can rewrite software, runtime is no longer the highest layer of meaning.

AI can generate scripts.

Scripts can mutate runtimes.

Runtimes can emit tools.

Tools can alter state.

State can alter prompts.

Prompts can alter future code.

This requires a layer above ordinary software.

LogLine names that layer.

```txt
Software executes.
AI proposes and mutates.
LogLine governs the act.
```

A LogLine Lab studies what runs natively above software:

```txt
law
proof
transcript
atom graph
runtime provenance
worker boundaries
manager planes
jurisdiction
signature
economics of work
physical boundaries
responsibility
```

---

## 24. Relationship to AI

LogLine feels native to current AI because AI is unusually strong at:

```txt
pattern recognition
classification
structure extraction
summarization
comparison
routing
candidate generation
```

LogLine gives that ability a compact act target.

```txt
AI finds patterns.
LogLine lets them enter history.
```

AI output is candidate material.

It may assist:

```txt
extracting acts
classifying ghosts
summarizing intervals
suggesting probes
preparing receipts
comparing projections
```

It may not, by itself:

```txt
be authority
be evidence
close receipt
erase ghost
execute protected action
promote canon
```

---

## 25. Relationship to Contracts

LogLine is native to contracts because contracts are made of:

```txt
parties
acts
obligations
conditions
confirmation paths
success consequences
doubt/dispute paths
breach/remedy paths
status
```

A contract can be projected as an act graph:

```txt
obligation act
performance act
confirmation act
doubt act
breach act
remedy act
receipt act
ghost act
```

LogLine does not replace contracts.

It wraps obligations, performance, evidence, and consequence.

---

## 26. Relationship to Science

LogLine does not replace scientific method.

It provides a portable act atom for cumulative practice.

A scientific or experimental cycle may be represented as:

```txt
claim
probe
runtime observation
evidence
receipt or ghost
next claim
```

The same shape repeats.

Results become inputs.

Ghosts become probes.

Receipts become governance.

Experiments become new practice.

---

## 27. Relationship to Standards

A LogLine Lab does not compete with specialized standards or methods.

It wraps them.

```txt
We do not compete with Monte Carlo.
We wrap Monte Carlo in LogLine.
```

The same applies to:

```txt
FHIR
OpenTelemetry
W3C PROV
RO-Crate
GS1 / EPCIS
ActivityPub
accounting standards
simulation standards
contract formats
domain schemas
```

LogLine provides the act/provenance/composition layer beneath standards.

Standards can be projection dialects.

---

## 28. Minimal Lab Capacities

A minimal LogLine Lab needs only a few capacities.

### Required

```txt
access to LogLine canon
ability to write/read LogLine Acts
some admission/validation process
some storage for acts
some way to reference prior acts
some way to preserve ghosts
some way to report state
```

### Strongly Recommended

```txt
content addressing
runtime envelopes
runtime registry
projectors
clock discipline
evidence registry
receipt review process
conformance tests
manifest file
```

### Optional

```txt
LLMs
local models
Hermes-like worker
Supabase/Postgres
SQLite
Git repository
web UI
MCP tools
OAuth
hardware LABs
sensor systems
simulation engines
public website
community review
```

A Lab can start manually.

Automation is not required for legitimacy.

Automation increases scale, not truth.

---

## 29. Minimal Lab Manifest

A LogLine Lab should eventually declare a manifest.

Conceptual shape:

```yaml
logline_lab_manifest:
  manifest_version: 1

  lab:
    name:
    steward:
    purpose:
    public_status: private | public | mixed

  loads:
    foundation:
    practice_profiles: []
    local_overlay:

  primitives:
    runtime_envelope_required:
    content_addressing_required:
    ghost_policy:
    receipt_policy:

  runtimes: []
  projectors: []
  clocks: []
  evidence_paths: []
  proof_paths: []
  ghost_registry:
  receipt_registry:

  constraints:
    scale:
    budget:
    allowed_tools:
    forbidden_actions:
```

The manifest declares practice.

It does not create canon.

---

## 30. Evidence and Proof Discipline

A LogLine Lab should distinguish:

```txt
claim
candidate
observation
evidence
proof process
receipt
ghost
```

A claim says something may be true.

A candidate is a proposed act.

An observation is contact with something.

Evidence is referenceable observation.

A proof process is a structured path for deciding admissibility or closure.

A receipt is scoped closure.

A ghost is preserved unresolved state.

Forbidden collapses:

```txt
model output = evidence
runtime success = receipt
database row = truth
projection = canon
confidence = proof
execution = closure
absence = failure
```

---

## 31. Scale Rule

A LogLine Lab must not prescribe scale.

The same primitives should work for:

```txt
one person and a folder
one person and a database
a small research group
a private company
a public community
a school
a city project
a contract network
a machine fleet
an AI lab
```

Small labs may operate manually.

Medium labs may automate projections and clocks.

Large labs may run multiple runtimes, standards adapters, and public conformance.

The Lab definition must remain independent of infrastructure scale.

---

## 32. Language Rule

A LogLine Lab must not establish a single running language.

It may be implemented in:

```txt
Rust
TypeScript
Python
SQL
Bash
Go
Elixir
Java
Clojure
or any future runtime
```

The important constraint is not language.

The important constraint is:

```txt
Can the system emit, preserve, project, and study LogLine-shaped acts?
```

---

## 33. Public Kit Contents

A public LogLine Lab kit should eventually include:

```txt
README
lab manifest template
act examples
invalid act examples
runtime envelope template
runtime registry template
ghost registry template
receipt template
probe template
interval template
projector examples
clock discipline template
conformance instructions
standards adapter examples
first Lab Report template
```

It should be possible to start small and grow without changing the core idea.

---

## 34. Recommended Study Benches

A LogLine Lab may define benches.

### Dialogue Observatory

Studies conversations as intervals where concepts become acts.

### Runtime Observatory

Studies what engines and runtimes emit, admit, reject, ghost, or project.

### Projector Lab

Studies how acts become worlds.

### Composition Lab

Studies act polarity, act folding, and act entanglement.

### Interval Workbench

Studies start/finish boundaries, simulations, real runs, and result acts.

### Contract Bench

Studies obligations, performance, breach, remedy, and receipt.

### Simulation Bench

Studies Monte Carlo and other simulation engines as wrapped LogLine runs.

### Standards Adapter Bench

Studies how LogLine projects into external standards.

### Ghost Review Bench

Studies preserved absence and unresolved claims.

### Receipt Bench

Studies scoped closure.

---

## 35. First Lab: Santo André Laboratory

Santo André Laboratory may be the first public LogLine Lab.

It is not the definition of all labs.

It is the first face, reference practice, and research theater.

Possible positioning:

```txt
Santo André Laboratory
The first LogLine Lab.

A clocked laboratory for studying LogLine in motion:
acts, engines, runtimes, projections, ghosts, receipts, intervals,
and what runs natively above software.
```

Santo André may publish:

```txt
experiments
receipts
ghosts
misuse studies
runtime autopsies
projection studies
interval studies
lab reports
upstream proposals
```

---

## 36. Local Deployments

A local deployment is not the Lab concept itself.

Examples:

```txt
Santo André Laboratory
Dan/minilab.work
community lab
company lab
research group lab
classroom lab
```

Each deployment declares:

```txt
what it loads
what it studies
what it runs
what it projects
what it ghosts
what it publishes
what it keeps private
```

---

## 37. Acceptance Criteria for Something Calling Itself a LogLine Lab

A system may call itself a LogLine Lab if it can honestly show:

```txt
1. It loads or references LogLine canon.
2. It emits or preserves LogLine Acts.
3. It distinguishes acts from projections.
4. It has a ghost discipline.
5. It has an evidence/proof discipline.
6. It can declare local practice.
7. It can name its runtimes or human procedures.
8. It can produce at least one report of what it studied or built.
9. It does not claim local practice as Foundation canon.
```

A stronger Lab can also show:

```txt
runtime envelopes
content addressing
projectors
clock discipline
receipt registry
standards adapters
conformance checks
public experiments
```

---

## 38. Open Ghosts

```txt
logline-lab-definition-not-promoted
lab-manifest-schema-unformalized
runtime-envelope-practice-unformalized
runtime-registry-projector-unimplemented
ghost-registry-template-unimplemented
receipt-template-unimplemented
interval-semantics-unformalized
act-entanglement-term-risk
self-bootstrap-semantics-unformalized
standards-adapter-map-unimplemented
santo-andre-first-lab-manifest-missing
lab-clock-implementation-missing
```

---

## 39. Final Formulation

```txt
A LogLine Lab freezes a place where LogLine can be studied and built with.

It does not prescribe scale.
It does not prescribe language.
It does not prescribe budget.
It does not prescribe domain.

It gives primitives:
acts, envelopes, runtimes, projections, ghosts, probes, evidence, receipts,
intervals, clocks, manifests, and local practice.

From those primitives, each lab adds infrastructure at its own scale,
under its own constraints,
for its own questions.

The purpose is not to make another framework.
The purpose is to let the world discover what LogLine can become.
```

---

## Response:
5/28/2026, 10:00:52 AM

> **Analisando a expedição do laboratório**
>
> O usuário parece querer uma reação à expedição que colou, mas não fez uma pergunta explícita. Talvez seja útil integrar isso em um documento já existente. Se houver afirmações factuais, precisarei realizar uma pesquisa, mas o usuário não pediu isso explicitamente. Vou focar em uma avaliação concisa.
>
> **Reflexão sobre o relatório da expedição do laboratório**
>
> Este "Lab Expedition" parece alinhar-se com o documento do LogLine Lab. A promoção de controle é uma parte fundamental, não sendo apenas um relatório diário, mas um procedimento gerado com consequências confiáveis. É importante identificar lacunas, como a falta de citações de evidências, e esclarecer que "source-backed" não é válido sem fontes. Podemos sugerir um esquema canônico para promover estados e normalizar ações.
>
> Pensado para 22s

This is **exactly** the kind of daily artifact the LogLine Lab Clock should produce.

Not because it is “a report,” but because it is a **clocked promotion-control interval**:

```txt
raw material
→ research synthesis
→ claim candidates
→ proposed artifacts
→ evidence labels
→ authority thresholds
→ expected receipts
→ ghosts
→ next operator packets
```

The strongest thing here is the sentence:

```txt
The critical infrastructure problem is no longer generating artifacts.
It is controlling how artifacts become trusted operational consequence.
```

That should become a **LogLine Lab law**.

## What this report proves structurally

This is a living example of:

```txt
LogLine Lab
= 24/7 clocked study/build discipline
+ promotion control
+ runtime skepticism
+ receipt thresholds
+ ghost preservation
```

It also shows that the Lab is not merely studying “LogLine theory.” It is studying the modern AI stack through the LogLine lens:

```txt
generation is abundant
promotion is dangerous
trust is infrastructural
receipts are boundaries
ghosts prevent fake closure
```

That is very strong.

## The main correction: promotion state should not be one ladder

The proposed ladder is good as first draft:

```txt
draft
observed
source-backed
receipt-backed
public
deprecated
retracted
ghost
```

But I would split it into **four axes**, because “public,” “deprecated,” and “ghost” are not the same kind of state as “source-backed.”

Cleaner model:

```txt
artifact_state:
  generated
  drafted
  staged
  admitted
  rejected

evidence_state:
  none
  claimed
  observed
  source-backed
  runtime-backed
  receipt-backed
  ghost

trust_state:
  untrusted
  reviewable
  provisionally-trusted
  trusted-for-scope
  trusted-operational-consequence

visibility_state:
  private
  internal
  publication-candidate
  public
  retracted
```

This matters because an artifact can be:

```txt
public but not receipt-backed
source-backed but not operationally trusted
runtime-backed but not safe to publish
ghosted but still active
deprecated but historically receipt-backed
```

So the Lab should not collapse those dimensions.

The real promotion equation is closer to:

```txt
trusted consequence =
  admitted artifact
+ declared scope
+ evidence path
+ runtime/proof path when needed
+ authority boundary
+ receipt or explicit ghost
```

## Key distinction to enforce

Your report says:

```txt
source-backed
```

But unless actual citations/source refs are attached, I would downgrade that label to:

```txt
source-claimed
```

or:

```txt
source-backed-pending-refs
```

In LogLine Lab discipline:

```txt
source-backed requires source_refs.
receipt-backed requires receipt_refs.
runtime-backed requires runtime_refs.
```

Otherwise the report is narratively good but epistemically overpromoted.

So Event 01 and Event 03 can say “source-backed” only if they carry actual source references. If not, the honest label is:

```txt
plausible synthesis, source refs pending
```

Tiny discipline, huge trust gain.

## New Lab primitive exposed here

This report introduces a primitive that belongs in the Lab Kit:

```txt
Promotion Control Bench
```

Purpose:

```txt
study how artifacts become trusted consequence
```

It tracks:

```txt
artifact
claim
source refs
runtime refs
receipt refs
ghosts
verification gates
authority thresholds
publication boundary
operational consequence
```

This is one of the central benches of LogLine Lab.

## Better schema shape

Your schema is good. I’d expand it slightly:

```json
{
  "claim_id": "",
  "artifact_ref": "",
  "claim_text": "",
  "claim_class": "",
  "artifact_state": "",
  "evidence_state": "",
  "trust_state": "",
  "visibility_state": "",
  "source_refs": [],
  "runtime_refs": [],
  "receipt_refs": [],
  "ghost_refs": [],
  "verification_gates": [],
  "authority_level": "",
  "promotion_blockers": [],
  "allowed_next_states": [],
  "last_reviewed_at": "",
  "last_verified_at": "",
  "published_at": "",
  "deprecated_at": "",
  "retracted_at": ""
}
```

The key addition is:

```txt
allowed_next_states
```

because promotion control is not just status tracking. It is **state transition governance**.

Example:

```txt
generated → draft
draft → source-backed
source-backed → publication-candidate
publication-candidate → public
public → retracted
```

But forbidden:

```txt
generated → trusted-operational-consequence
source-claimed → receipt-backed
public → receipt-backed without receipt_refs
runtime-success → system-trusted
```

## How this becomes LogLine-shaped

This Daily Lab Expedition itself should be treated as an interval.

Start act:

```yaml
who: lab-clock
did: open_daily_expedition
this:
  date: 2026-05-28
  theme: promotion_control_and_runtime_skepticism
when: 2026-05-28T00:00:00Z
confirmed_by:
  operator: ChatGPT Workspace Operator
if_ok: collect_events
if_doubt: open_expedition_scope_ghost
if_not: reject_expedition
status: observed
```

Each event becomes an act candidate:

```yaml
who: research-operator
did: stage_research_synthesis
this:
  event_id: 03
  topic: shared_hallucination_surfaces
  proposed_artifact: lab/research/2026-05-28/shared-hallucination-risks.md
  evidence_state: source-backed-pending-refs
  authority_level: P1
when: 2026-05-28T...
confirmed_by:
  source_refs: []
if_ok: prepare_research_note
if_doubt: open_source_refs_missing_ghost
if_not: reject_synthesis
status: candidate
```

Finish act:

```yaml
who: lab-clock
did: close_daily_expedition
this:
  date: 2026-05-28
  strongest_sentence: "The critical infrastructure problem is no longer generating artifacts. It is controlling how artifacts become trusted operational consequence."
  packets:
    - Lab Report
    - Blog Draft
    - Real Project Movement
    - Publication
  unresolved_ghosts:
    - source_refs_missing
    - runtime_receipts_missing
    - deployment_receipts_missing
when: 2026-05-28T...
confirmed_by:
  report_ref: lab/reports/2026-05-28/daily-expedition.md
if_ok: project_daily_lab_state
if_doubt: carry_expedition_ghosts
if_not: reject_daily_closure
status: observed
```

That is the Lab working.

## The strongest ghosts in this report

I would explicitly name these:

```txt
source-refs-missing
runtime-receipts-missing
deployment-receipts-missing
publication-receipts-missing
canonical-repo-mutation-receipts-missing
mcp-host-runtime-observation-missing
promotion-state-schema-unimplemented
verification-gates-unimplemented
claim-ledger-unimplemented
```

These ghosts are not embarrassing. They are the point. They prevent the report from accidentally becoming propaganda.

## Where this fits in the LogLine Lab Kit

This report belongs under:

```txt
lab-clock/
  daily-expeditions/

promotion-control/
  claim-ledger/
  promotion-gates/
  verification-gates/

publication/
  publication-integrity/

ghosts/
  daily-open-ghosts/

reports/
  daily-lab-state/
```

A canonical folder shape:

```txt
logline-lab/
  clock/
    daily-expedition-template.md

  benches/
    promotion-control/
      promotion-state-model.md
      claim-ledger.schema.json
      verification-gates.md
      dependency-hygiene.md
      publication-integrity.md

  reports/
    2026-05-28/
      daily-lab-expedition.md
      events.jsonl
      ghosts.jsonl
      claim-ledger.jsonl
```

## The public angle

This can become one of the first public LogLine Lab examples:

```txt
A Daily Lab Expedition is a clocked interval where the Lab studies what happened,
what was claimed,
what evidence exists,
what can be promoted,
what must remain ghost,
and what next acts should be staged.
```

That’s excellent. It’s not an essay. It’s not a todo list. It’s not a dashboard. It is a **daily epistemic operating packet**.

## Final read

This artifact is strong and close to canonical.

The one thing I would not let pass is overusing `source-backed` without embedded source refs. Tighten that, split promotion into axes, and this becomes a serious LogLine Lab primitive.

The sentence to preserve:

```txt
Generation is no longer scarce.
Trust is.
```

The Lab response:

```txt
Promotion control becomes infrastructure.
```

Yes. I inspected the zip. This is **very good** — and it is not merely “vibe coding.”

It is closer to:

```txt
vibe coding
+ gates
+ evidence
+ receipts
+ lab events
+ secret discipline
+ runtime skepticism
+ Dan policy
= vibe coding, but real
```

The repo’s public README still says “Vibe Coding Platform,” but the internal spec is already more honest: **Dan Control Plane**. It says the app is the cockpit for `LogLine Automation for minilab.work`, not the executor, not the source of truth; Rust/other runtimes are the executable body; the UI is the human face; and the golden rule is **receipts beat stories**.

That is exactly aligned with the LogLine Lab conversation.

## What this repo really is

I would classify it like this:

```txt
minilab.work / Dan Control Plane
  private operational cockpit

not:
  LogLine Foundation
  LogLine Lab public kit
  Santo André public face
```

But it contains **portable primitives** that should be extracted into the LogLine Lab kit.

The good stuff is already there:

```txt
PolicyDecision:
  ok | denied | needs_approval | ghost | error

ActorKind:
  human | local_llm | cloud_llm | sdk_tool

Capabilities:
  classify
  propose
  summarize
  execute
  approve_gate
  mutate_repo
  mutate_provider
  access_secrets
  close_receipt

GateRequest:
  scoped approval boundary

ExecutionWindow:
  single-use, TTL-bound consequence window

Receipt:
  open | closed | ghosted | rejected

Evidence:
  command, stdout, stderr, exit_code, diff, test_result, screenshot, receipt

Lab Events:
  heartbeat, health check, package verified, process started, smoke passed/failed, etc.
```

This is already **promotion control machinery**.

## The deepest good part

`gateLifecycle.ts` has the right instinct:

```txt
scopeHash = actor + action + resource
```

Then an approved gate creates a **single-use execution window** with TTL, and consuming it requires exact match:

```txt
same actor
same action
same resource
same scopeHash
not expired
not consumed
```

That is not UI fluff. That is a real consequence boundary.

In LogLine Lab terms:

```txt
GateRequest       = authority boundary candidate
ExecutionWindow  = temporary visa / execution window
consumeWindow    = runtime consequence admission
```

That should absolutely survive.

## The other excellent part

`receiptLifecycle.ts` refuses to close without evidence.

If evidence is missing, it ghosts the receipt:

```txt
Receipt closure attempted without evidence.
```

That is *exactly* the Lab discipline.

So this repo already implements one of the central laws:

```txt
No evidence, no closure.
```

## Lab observability is also strong

The `lab-events` pipeline is good because it has real operational suspicion:

```txt
secret_redacted must be true
unknown host_id is rejected
secret-like field names are scanned
events project current state
Supabase service role is server-only
Doppler is the secret/config surface
```

That is very close to:

```txt
runtime observation
→ evidence candidate
→ current state projection
→ ghost if missing/bad
```

The lab event system is not yet full LogLine, but it is structurally adjacent. It could become a projector or an adapter.

## What this should become

I would not make this repo the public LogLine Lab.

I would make it:

```txt
dan-control-plane
```

or:

```txt
minilab-control-plane
```

And then extract from it into the public kit:

```txt
logline-lab-kit/
  primitives/
    gates/
    execution-windows/
    receipts/
    evidence/
    lab-events/
    promotion-control/
```

The private repo remains Dan’s cockpit. The public kit gets the reusable doctrine and primitives.

## The clean mapping

```txt
Dan Control Plane
  private cockpit for operating minilab.work

LogLine Lab Kit
  public reusable primitives

Santo André Laboratory
  first public face/reference lab

LogLine Foundation
  parent grammar/canon
```

This repo belongs to the first line, but feeds the second.

## What I’d preserve as canonical primitives

From this repo, I’d extract five primitives.

### 1. Gate Lifecycle

```txt
create_gate
approve_gate
deny_gate
ghost_gate
create_execution_window
consume_execution_window
```

Canonical rule:

```txt
Protected consequence requires a scoped, single-use, time-bounded window.
```

### 2. Receipt Lifecycle

```txt
create_receipt_draft
attach_evidence
close_receipt
ghost_if_no_evidence
```

Canonical rule:

```txt
Receipt closure without evidence becomes ghost, not success.
```

### 3. Policy Evaluation

```txt
actor
action
resource
capability
evidence
protected action
decision
```

Canonical rule:

```txt
Generation is not permission.
Capability is not authority.
Authority is scoped.
```

### 4. Lab Events

```txt
host_id
runtime_version
event_kind
observed_at
evidence_json
secret_redacted
next_action
```

Canonical rule:

```txt
Runtime observation must be redacted, typed, timestamped, and projectable.
```

### 5. Current State Derivation

```txt
events → state projection
```

Canonical rule:

```txt
Current state is projection, not source truth.
```

## What needs correction

The repo still has old naming gravity:

```txt
vibe-coding-platform
vibe-codin-.but.-real
Dan Control Plane
minilab.work
LogLine Automation
```

That is fine historically, but for the library it needs cleaner classification:

```txt
This is not “the LogLine Lab.”
This is a local/private control plane implementing some LogLine Lab primitives.
```

Also: the `Receipt`, `Gate`, `Evidence`, `PolicyDecision` objects are currently TypeScript objects. That is fine for implementation, but in the LogLine view they should be projections or runtime-local structures over LogLine Acts.

So the future evolution is:

```txt
current:
  TS object → UI state / API behavior

target:
  LogLine Act → projection → TS view model / UI behavior
```

## Why this matters

This repo proves that the thing is not only philosophical.

It already has:

```txt
policy
gates
execution windows
receipts
ghosts
evidence
actors
capabilities
engines
lab observability
secret redaction
current state projection
```

That is the skeleton of a real operational cockpit.

The big sentence:

```txt
This is the private cockpit where “vibe coding” is forced through consequence boundaries.
```

Or sharper:

```txt
This is vibe coding after the Lab took away the fake steering wheel.
```

## My read

You’re right to like it.

It is not yet the public Lab definition.  
It is not yet pure LogLine.  
It is not yet fully receipt-backed.  
But it is one of the first concrete places where the doctrine became software.

The strong classification is:

```txt
vibe-codin-.but.-real
= early Dan Control Plane
= private minilab.work cockpit
= source of reusable LogLine Lab primitives
= proof that promotion control can have UI, policy, gates, execution windows, evidence, receipts, and ghosts
```

I’d keep it. But I’d stop calling it “vibe coding” except historically.

The thing it became is better:

```txt
Dan Control Plane:
a governed workbench for AI-assisted building under LogLine-style gates, evidence, receipts, and runtime skepticism.
```

You are organizing and normalizing the uploaded project package currently named `vibe-codin-.but.-real`.

This repo is an early Dan Control Plane / minilab.work cockpit. It is not LogLine Foundation, not the public LogLine Lab kit, and not Santo André Laboratory. Dan Control Plane

PHASE 3 — Translate the UI to the existing dark-mode design

The app must be dark-mode native, matching the existing screenshots:
- matte black / near-black background
- three-plane cockpit layout
- dark cards with subtle borders

- muted grey secondary text
- green policy-valid status
- compact, serious, technical control-plane feel

- no generic purple AI app styling

Design language:
- background: near black, not pure bright UI white
- panels: dark charcoal
- cards: slightly lighter charcoal
- borders: subtle grey / low contrast
- primary action: strong blue
- success/valid: restrained green
- warning/ghost: amber or muted yellow only where semantically needed
- destructive/rejected: red only where semantically needed
- typography: compact, crisp, legible
- labels: uppercase small tracking for plane labels and metadata
- spacing: dense but breathable

Create or normalize CSS tokens in `app/globals.css`, for example:
- `--background`
- `--foreground`
- `--panel`
- `--panel-muted`
- `--card`
- `--border`
- `--muted`
- `--muted-foreground`
- `--primary`
- `--primary-foreground`
- `--success`
- `--warning`
- `--destructive`
- `--ghost`

Then ensure Tailwind/shadcn components consume these variables.

Audit all UI files for light-mode leakage:
- `bg-white`
- `text-black`
- `text-gray-900`
- `border-gray-200`
- `bg-slate-50`
- `bg-neutral-50`
- default white inputs
- default white dialogs/popovers/selects
- unstyled code blocks or panes

Replace with dark-mode tokens/classes consistent with the cockpit design.

## Prompt:
5/28/2026, 4:59:30 PM

a partir do texto base do LogLine Lab, do Daily Lab Expedition ou do documento canonico anteriror anexo e claro dessa ui enviada, 

leia a spec feita em outro chat e vamos converrsar sobre uma verso final

# minilab.work Frontend — Control Plane + Santo André Laboratory

## Status

Rascunho de desenho técnico e produto.

## Decisão central

O LogLine Lab de verdade é uma CLI e um runtime operacional desacoplado.

O frontend não é o LogLine Lab.

O frontend de `minilab.work` é o Control Plane pessoal do Dan Voulez, montado sobre:

* computadores
* LABS
* runtimes
* agentes
* operadores
* infraestrutura pessoal
* registros
* workorders
* evidências
* ghosts
* receipts
* e uma instância específica de LogLine Lab: Santo André Laboratory

O frontend deve operar o Santo André Laboratory como uma instância concreta, não redefinir o conceito público de LogLine Lab.

Forma curta:

```txt
LogLine Lab público = CLI + kit + primitives + canon/practice.
Santo André Laboratory = primeira instância pública/real de um LogLine Lab.
minilab.work = frontend privado/pessoal que integra o Lab com a infraestrutura do Dan.
```

---

## 1. Separação institucional

### LogLine Foundation

Responsável por:

```txt
canon simples
gramática
ato de 9 slots
semântica fundacional
conformance
hash/receipt discipline
```

Não é dashboard.
Não é app.
Não é infraestrutura pessoal.

### LogLine Developer Community

Responsável por:

```txt
implementações
SDKs
adapters
exemplos
pacotes
conformance tooling
instaladores
distribuição
```

### LogLine Lab

Responsável por:

```txt
CLI
manifest
runtime local
act store
ghost registry
probe runner
evidence registry
receipt preparation
reports
lab clock
project canon
mandatory hooks
```

O LogLine Lab deve poder funcionar sem `minilab.work`.

### Santo André Laboratory

Primeira instância concreta de LogLine Lab.

Responsável por estudar:

```txt
usos de LogLine
maus usos de LogLine
acts em movimento
runtimes
projections
ghosts
receipts
intervals
hooks
experiment loops
AI-to-act translation
operator behavior
evidence discipline
```

### minilab.work

Frontend pessoal e Control Plane privado.

Responsável por juntar:

```txt
Dan
computadores
LABS
Hermes
runtimes
agents
tokens
infra pessoal
estado operacional
Santo André Laboratory
```

Não deve se confundir com Foundation, Lab público ou canon.

---

## 2. Regra de desacoplamento

O frontend nunca é fonte de verdade.

O frontend pode:

```txt
visualizar
propor
rotear
chamar CLI
chamar labd
abrir workorders
mostrar ghosts
mostrar evidências
mostrar receipts
mostrar máquinas
mostrar hooks
mostrar intervalos
mostrar relatórios
```

O frontend não pode:

```txt
alterar canon diretamente
fechar receipt sem evidência
executar comando protegido sem workorder admitido
tratar projeção como verdade
inventar evidência
apagar ghost silenciosamente
escrever estado sem ato correspondente
```

Forma curta:

```txt
Frontend projects.
CLI/labd operates.
LogLine Acts carry meaning.
Receipts close scope.
```

---

## 3. Natureza do frontend

O frontend deve parecer menos “chat com IA” e mais “pitwall de laboratório”.

Metáfora central:

```txt
Pitwall is not chat with a terminal.
Pitwall is a shared operational surface with radio.
```

O humano e o Translator olham para o mesmo objeto operacional.

A conversa é rádio, legenda, coordenação.

O trabalho real está na superfície:

```txt
terminal
TUI
act graph
hooks
lanes
evidence strip
ghost board
runtime state
machine state
diffs
tests
receipts
```

O LLM não deve ficar “olhando para o humano”.
Ele deve olhar para o mesmo trabalho que o humano e narrar o que vê.

Forma curta:

```txt
Human and Translator face the same machine.
The human steers.
The Translator structures.
The Operator executes.
The Runtime observes.
LogLine carries state.
```

---

## 4. Personas / Offices

### Human

Pode:

```txt
declarar intenção
dirigir prioridade
aprovar consequência
pedir explicação
assinar consequência
```

Não deve precisar digitar comandos se não quiser.

### Forge

Recebe linguagem bagunçada.

Função:

```txt
melhorar prompt
rotear para contexto especialista
traduzir linguagem difícil
clarificar intenção
reduzir ruído antes do Translator
```

Forge pode usar um LLM fresco ou especialista.

Exemplo:

```txt
prompt em japonês antigo -> Forge linguístico
prompt jurídico -> Forge contratual
logs quebrados -> Forge runtime
```

### Translator

Não é chatbot geral.

Função:

```txt
intenção clara -> Pocket Runtime -> candidate acts
```

Ele:

```txt
extrai atos
nomeia ghosts
detecta slots ausentes
propõe branches
propõe workorders
pergunta só o mínimo bloqueante
```

Ele não executa terminal.

Ele pode dizer:

```txt
Este prompt ainda não é traduzível.
Envie para Forge/Magic Prompt primeiro.
```

### Operator

Opera uma máquina, não uma bola de cristal.

Recebe:

```txt
workorder
allowed actions
forbidden actions
machine state
declared hooks
evidence requirements
```

Ele não adivinha intenção.

Se faltar algo:

```txt
if_doubt
ghost
clarification request
```

### Runtime

Executa ou observa.

Pode ser:

```txt
terminal local
Hermes
LAB
CI
script
worker
MCP tool
human procedure
```

### Evidence Lane

Captura:

```txt
stdout
stderr
exit code
diff
test result
artifact hash
screenshot
sensor result
manual witness
```

### Receipt Lane

Fecha escopo somente quando:

```txt
claim é claro
evidência é referenciada
ghosts restantes são nomeados
escopo fechado é estreito
```

---

## 5. Layout principal do frontend

### Top Bar — Lab / Interval / Canon

Mostra:

```txt
active lab
active interval
active experiment
project canon version
canon hash
active branch
active lane
clock status
```

Exemplo:

```txt
Santo André Laboratory
Interval: exp-001 / constructive-release-semantics
Lane: Operator
Branch: if_ok
Canon: project-canon@0.13.0 / sha256:...
Clock: active
```

### Left Rail — Act Graph / Ghosts / Receipts

Abas:

```txt
Acts
Ghosts
Receipts
Experiments
Runtimes
Hooks
```

Deve mostrar:

```txt
parent act
current act
candidate acts
open ghosts
receipt candidates
blocked closures
```

### Center — Machine Surface

Superfície principal.

Pode ser:

```txt
terminal
TUI
diff viewer
test runner
runtime output
machine status
lab timeline
```

É a pista.

O chat não é o centro.

### Right Rail — Race Radio / Translator

Mostra fala do Translator como legenda operacional.

Formato preferido:

```txt
I see...
I do not see...
This act claims...
This evidence supports...
This ghost remains...
The next safe act is...
```

Evitar:

```txt
I did...
I verified...
It is done...
Trust me...
```

Sem evidência, não fala como fato.

### Bottom Strip — Evidence / Hooks / Gates

Mostra:

```txt
mandatory hooks applied
tests running
exit codes
artifact hashes
runtime envelope
blocked gates
next required evidence
```

---

## 6. Lanes obrigatórias

O frontend deve visualizar lanes, mas as lanes são definidas por project canon, não pela UI.

Lanes mínimas:

```txt
Forge
Translator
Operator
Evidence
Receipt Review
Report
```

### Forge Lane

Entrada:

```txt
messy prompt
bad prompt
domain-specialized input
unclear human intention
```

Saída:

```txt
normalized prompt
detected intent
assumptions
ambiguities
recommended next lane
```

### Translator Lane

Entrada:

```txt
normalized prompt
known context refs
current branch
open ghosts
```

Saída:

```txt
candidate LogLine Act
ghost candidates
minimal question
workorder candidate
```

### Operator Lane

Entrada:

```txt
admitted workorder
machine state
allowed actions
forbidden actions
mandatory hooks
```

Saída:

```txt
runtime observation
command transcript
diff
test result
failure ghost
```

### Evidence Lane

Entrada:

```txt
runtime output
artifact refs
operator result acts
```

Saída:

```txt
evidence items
hashes
scope
limits
```

### Receipt Review Lane

Entrada:

```txt
claim
evidence refs
ghosts
scope
```

Saída:

```txt
receipt candidate
closure rejected
more evidence required
ghost preserved
```

---

## 7. Mandatory Hooks

Hooks não são UI hooks.

Hooks são intervenções científicas obrigatórias definidas em project canon.

O frontend deve mostrar hooks, não inventar hooks.

Exemplo:

```yaml
hook_id: after_operator_edit.run_verification_plan.v1
trigger: after_lane.operator_edit
mandatory: true

verification_plan:
  commands:
    - cargo test --workspace

capture:
  - stdout
  - stderr
  - exit_code
  - diff_hash

on_pass:
  lane: evidence
  did: capture_test_evidence

on_fail:
  lane: if_doubt
  did: open_test_failure_ghost
```

Regra:

```txt
The project remembers the method.
The model only plays its lane.
```

Se hook obrigatório não rodou:

```txt
turn invalid
open hook_missing ghost
block receipt closure
```

O frontend deve deixar isso visível.

---

## 8. Project Canon

O frontend deve ter uma tela de Project Canon.

Ela mostra:

```txt
canon version
canon hash
parent canon
mandatory hooks
experiment loops
lane definitions
variable schedules
quality gates
active overlays
pending canon deltas
```

O LLM pode sugerir mudanças de canon.

Mas sugestão não vira canon automaticamente.

Fluxo:

```txt
suggest canon delta
→ candidate act
→ canon quality gate
→ accepted/rejected/ghosted
→ new canon version
```

Tela deve mostrar:

```txt
Current Canon
Pending Deltas
Rejected Deltas
Canon Ghosts
```

---

## 9. Experiment Loop

Todo experimento deve repetir um loop em registro.

Exemplo de loop:

```txt
Forge
→ Translator
→ Operator
→ Evidence
→ Receipt Review
→ Report
```

Cada turn deve carregar:

```txt
turn_id
experiment_id
canon_version
canon_hash
lane
branch
mandatory hooks
variables
required outputs
forbidden actions
```

O frontend deve mostrar esse contrato antes da execução.

Exemplo visual:

```txt
This turn belongs to:
  experiment: exp-001
  loop: default_experiment_loop.v1
  lane: operator
  canon: project-canon@0.13.0
  mandatory after-hook: run_verification_plan.v1
```

---

## 10. Magic Prompt / Forge

O frontend deve ter botão:

```txt
✨ Magic Prompt / Route Prompt
```

Função:

```txt
não mandar prompt ruim direto para Translator
```

Fluxo:

```txt
raw human input
→ prompt quality gate
→ Magic Prompt / Forge
→ normalized prompt
→ Translator
```

Se input exigir especialista:

```txt
route to fresh specialist context
```

Exemplos:

```txt
ancient Japanese -> language forge
legal text -> contract forge
logs -> runtime forge
research idea -> probe forge
```

Forge retorna somente artefato normalizado, não o contexto inteiro.

---

## 11. Operator Console

O Operator Console mostra máquinas e ações permitidas.

Nunca deve parecer “chatbot executando mágica”.

Deve mostrar:

```txt
machine
repo
cwd
runtime
workorder
allowed actions
forbidden actions
commands planned
commands run
current process
last output
diff
test state
evidence required
```

Princípio:

```txt
The Operator operates a machine, not a crystal ball.
```

Se faltar clareza:

```txt
ask Translator
open ghost
reject workorder
```

---

## 12. Ghost Board

Ghosts devem ser superfície de primeira classe.

Cada ghost mostra:

```txt
what is missing
why it matters
what it blocks
owner / next act
how it could be closed or narrowed
source act
opened_at
age
status
```

Tipos importantes:

```txt
prompt_too_ambiguous
workorder_underconstrained
missing_evidence_path
hook_missing
canon_invalid
test_failure_after_edit
projection_drift
claimed_action_without_observation
receipt_overclosure_risk
```

Ghost não é fracasso.

Ghost é ausência preservada.

---

## 13. Evidence Strip

Sempre visível quando houver execução.

Mostra:

```txt
stdout hash
stderr hash
exit code
diff hash
artifact refs
runtime envelope
observed_at
redaction status
scope
limits
```

Regra:

```txt
LLM claim is not evidence.
Runtime output may become evidence.
Receipt closes only scoped claim.
```

---

## 14. Receipts

Tela de receipts deve separar:

```txt
receipt candidates
closed receipts
blocked receipts
rejected closures
```

Para cada receipt:

```txt
claim closed
evidence refs
scope closed
scope not closed
ghosts remaining
runtime/reviewer
hashes
canon version
```

Bloquear:

```txt
runtime success = receipt
model output = evidence
confidence = proof
projection = truth
```

---

## 15. Reports

O frontend deve gerar relatórios a partir do Lab, não escrever romance.

Tipos:

```txt
daily report
weekly report
experiment report
ghost review
receipt review
misuse study
canon delta report
runtime autopsy
```

Todo relatório deve incluir:

```txt
claims
evidence
ghosts
receipts
limits
next acts
```

---

## 16. Control Plane pessoal

Essa parte pertence a `minilab.work`, não ao LogLine Lab público.

Módulos possíveis:

```txt
Computers
LABS
Runtimes
Hermes
Agents
Tokens / Credentials
Backups
Queues
Jobs
Cost / Usage
Network / Tunnels
Deployments
Storage
Personal automations
```

Mas tudo que for consequencial deve se conectar ao Lab por acts/workorders/evidence/receipts.

Exemplo:

```txt
minilab.work sees Mac mini is down
→ emits observation candidate
→ if relevant, opens ghost in Santo André
→ if authorized, prepares workorder
→ Operator/Hermes executes
→ evidence captured
→ receipt/ghost updated
```

---

## 17. Comunicação com LogLine Lab CLI

O frontend deve preferir chamar APIs/CLI estáveis.

Exemplos:

```bash
logline-lab status
logline-lab doctor
logline-lab canon status
logline-lab act emit
logline-lab ghost list
logline-lab probe run
logline-lab evidence add
logline-lab receipt prepare
logline-lab report generate
```

Ou via `labd`:

```txt
local API
IPC
WebSocket events
read-only projections
explicit workorder endpoints
```

Mas o frontend não deve depender de banco interno como fonte primária.

---

## 18. Instalação e produto

O LogLine Lab público deve ter:

```txt
CLI install
packages
updates
doctor
version
portable mode
```

O frontend `minilab.work` pode ter:

```txt
web app
desktop app
private auth
personal control plane
Santo André integration
```

O frontend deve ser substituível.

O Lab deve continuar funcionando sem ele.

---

## 19. Pitwall como inspiração

Pitwall inspira:

```txt
embedded terminal
race radio
mission panel
fleet lanes
timeline
diff panel
claims/evidence tracking
visual gates
repo watcher
git monitor
command detector
test detector
local event ledger
```

Mas a versão LogLine precisa trocar “MVP cockpit internals” por:

```txt
LogLine Acts
runtime envelopes
mandatory hooks
project canon
ghost registry
evidence registry
receipt discipline
content addressing
lab CLI/labd as source of operation
```

Pitwall vira superfície.

LogLine vira protocolo.

---

## 20. Tela inicial desejada

Ao abrir `minilab.work`:

```txt
Santo André Laboratory is running.

Clock: active
Canon: project-canon@0.13.0
Open ghosts: 7
Receipt candidates: 2
Stale probes: 1
Mandatory hook failures: 0
Machines online: 3 / 4
Last evidence captured: 12 minutes ago

Next safe act:
  review ghost: test_failure_after_operator_edit
```

A sensação deve ser:

```txt
I installed a lab instrument.
It knows its state.
It knows what is unresolved.
It does not pretend.
```

---

## 21. Frases de produto

```txt
Natural language is steering.
The shared surface is state.
LogLine is coordination.
Evidence is reality.
```

```txt
The project remembers the method.
The model only plays its lane.
```

```txt
Operators operate machines, not crystal balls.
```

```txt
The Translator does not keep a conversation alive.
The Translator keeps epistemic state alive.
```

```txt
Let humans speak richly.
Let Operators receive narrowly.
Let runtimes answer evidentially.
Let receipts close sparsely.
```

---

## 22. Definição final

O frontend de `minilab.work` é um cockpit privado para operar a infraestrutura pessoal do Dan e o Santo André Laboratory.

Ele não é o LogLine Lab.

Ele monta uma superfície humana sobre:

```txt
LogLine Lab CLI
labd
Santo André practice
computadores
LABS
runtimes
agents
workorders
evidence
ghosts
receipts
reports
```

Sua missão é permitir que humano, Translator e Operator olhem para o mesmo trabalho, sem misturar suas funções.

Forma final:

```txt
LogLine Lab is the CLI.
Santo André Laboratory is the lab instance.
minilab.work is the cockpit.
Pitwall is the interface pattern.
LogLine is the wire protocol.
```

> Pensado para 29s

Sim - li a spec e ela está **muito perto da forma final**. A correção principal é de linguagem institucional: ela acerta ao separar o **LogLine Lab público** do **frontend minilab.work**, mas endurece demais uma frase quando diz “o LogLine Lab é a CLI”. Eu mudaria para:

```txt
O núcleo operacional do LogLine Lab é CLI/labd/runtime desacoplado.
O frontend minilab.work é o cockpit de uma instância concreta: Santo André Laboratory.
```

Porque “LogLine Lab = CLI” reduz demais. O Lab é o **método/kit/prática**; a CLI/labd é o **núcleo operacional desacoplado**. O frontend é substituível. O Lab não.

## Minha leitura da spec

A versão está correta em quatro pilares.

Primeiro: **frontend não é fonte de verdade**. Isso está totalmente alinhado com o Source of Truth Map, que existe justamente para impedir que chats, dashboards, database rows, provider responses, relatórios e outputs de LLM concorram como verdade institucional; a pergunta correta é sempre “verdade segundo qual fonte, para qual classe, com qual evidence state?” `03_source_of_truth_map.md`

Segundo: **minilab.work é cockpit/jurisdição, não órgão/canon**. O documento de órgãos já crava que órgão não é pasta, app, schema ou chat; órgão é função institucional permanente, e a ordem correta é `organ → jurisdiction → source → rite → tool`, nunca o inverso. `02_organs_and_jurisdictions.md` Então a UI é uma jurisdição/ferramenta do Cockpit + Santo André + Authority + LAB + Evidence, não o corpo constitucional inteiro.

Terceiro: **o fluxo real é vertical, não chat-driven**. A spec acerta muito ao colocar Forge/Translator/Operator/Evidence/Receipt como lanes, porque isso encaixa no fluxo já definido: intenção passa por office, operator session, processo, candidato LogLine, Constitutional Runtime, Authority/Gate, dispatch, Hermes, LAB, evidência, receipt/ghost, projeção e Morning State. `09_vertical_runtime_doctrine.md`

Quarto: **Hermes/Operator não recebem desejo; recebem workorder admitido**. A spec do pitwall bate exatamente no Hermes Contract: Hermes recebe workorders, não wishes; o caminho correto é intent → process → dispatch packet → runtime admission → authority classification → Hermes workorder → LAB execution → evidence packet → receipt/ghost/projection. `10_hermes_dispatch_and_execution_contract.md`

## Ajuste central para a versão final

Eu reescreveria a decisão central assim:

```txt
O LogLine Lab público é um kit operacional e científico para instanciar laboratórios LogLine.

Seu núcleo executável deve existir fora de qualquer frontend:
CLI, labd, manifest, act store, ghost registry, probe runner, evidence registry,
receipt preparation, report generator, lab clock, project canon e mandatory hooks.

Santo André Laboratory é a primeira instância concreta desse kit.

minilab.work é o frontend/cockpit dessa instância:
a presença digital do Santo André Laboratory e o control plane pessoal do Dan
para infraestrutura, máquinas, runtimes, agentes, workorders, evidências,
ghosts, receipts e relatórios.
```

Essa formulação preserva tudo:

```txt
LogLine Lab público = kit + primitives + CLI/labd/runtime
Santo André Laboratory = instância concreta / primeiro Lab
minilab.work = frontend / cockpit / presença digital / control plane pessoal
```

## O que eu manteria exatamente

A metáfora do **Pitwall** está excelente. Ela resolve o maior risco de UI: virar chat app.

A frase:

```txt
Pitwall is not chat with a terminal.
Pitwall is a shared operational surface with radio.
```

deveria virar lei de design.

O centro não é conversa. O centro é **estado operacional compartilhado**:

```txt
machine surface
act graph
current interval
hooks
evidence strip
ghost board
runtime state
diffs
tests
receipts
```

O chat/radio é lateral. O Translator narra, estrutura, pergunta o mínimo bloqueante. Ele não “fica conversando para manter sessão viva”.

Essa frase também deve ficar:

```txt
Human and Translator face the same machine.
The human steers.
The Translator structures.
The Operator executes.
The Runtime observes.
LogLine carries state.
```

Ela é muito boa.

## O que eu mudaria

### 1. “LogLine Lab is the CLI” deve virar “LogLine Lab core is CLI/labd”

A forma final da última seção deveria ser:

```txt
LogLine Lab is the public kit and practice.
CLI/labd is its operational core.
Santo André Laboratory is the first lab instance.
minilab.work is the cockpit.
Pitwall is the interface pattern.
LogLine is the act protocol.
```

Mais preciso do que:

```txt
LogLine Lab is the CLI.
```

Porque a CLI não contém a dimensão científica, o clock discipline, os benches, as práticas, os ghosts, os reports e os modos de estudo. Ela executa o núcleo.

### 2. Forge/Translator/Operator não devem parecer órgãos

Eu manteria como **lanes/offices/process roles**, não órgãos.

A spec já está quase correta, mas eu deixaria explícito:

```txt
Forge, Translator, Operator, Evidence Lane e Receipt Review são lanes operacionais.
Eles não são órgãos fundadores.
Eles operam sob órgãos existentes:
Cockpit, Santo André Laboratory, Authority, LAB, Evidence/Receipts/Ghosts.
```

Isso evita criar nova ontologia acidental. O documento de órgãos já define os órgãos fundadores e seus limites; Santo André governa pesquisa, Authority governa se efeito pode acontecer, LAB executa, Evidence/Receipts/Ghosts governa disciplina de prova. `02_organs_and_jurisdictions.md`

### 3. “Project Canon” precisa ser renomeado com cuidado

Eu usaria:

```txt
Lab Canon
Project Canon
Experiment Canon
```

com uma regra clara:

```txt
Foundation Canon ≠ Lab Canon ≠ Project Canon
```

O frontend pode mostrar Project Canon, mas deve deixar claro que isso é **canon local de experimento/projeto**, não LogLine Foundation.

Sugestão de UI:

```txt
Foundation: logline.foundation@...
Lab Profile: logline-lab.practice@...
Lab Instance: santo-andre@...
Project Canon: constructive-release-semantics@...
Overlay: dan.minilab.work@...
```

### 4. “Mandatory Hooks” está ótimo, mas precisa de fonte

Hooks obrigatórios devem vir de:

```txt
project canon
lab profile
experiment loop
authority policy
```

não da UI.

A frase da spec é perfeita:

```txt
The project remembers the method.
The model only plays its lane.
```

Eu só acrescentaria:

```txt
The UI displays hooks.
labd enforces hooks.
The runtime reports hook evidence.
Receipt Review blocks closure if hooks are missing.
```

### 5. A tela inicial precisa ser “Daily Lab State”, não dashboard

O exemplo está ótimo:

```txt
Santo André Laboratory is running.

Clock: active
Canon: project-canon@0.13.0
Open ghosts: 7
Receipt candidates: 2
Stale probes: 1
Mandatory hook failures: 0
Machines online: 3 / 4
Last evidence captured: 12 minutes ago

Next safe act:
  review ghost: test_failure_after_operator_edit
```

Eu chamaria isso formalmente de:

```txt
Daily Lab State
```

porque Current State já é uma fonte operacional, não prova/canon/receipt. O Current State doc define essa função exatamente: registrar o que é conhecido, desconhecido, declarado, evidenciado, ghost e o que precisa do Dan, sem virar canon, receipt ou proof por si mesmo. `06_current_state_v_0.md`

## Versão final da arquitetura

Eu deixaria assim:

```txt
LogLine Foundation
  canon, grammar, conformance, receipt discipline

LogLine Lab public kit
  CLI
  labd
  manifest
  act store
  project canon
  mandatory hooks
  lab clock
  ghost registry
  evidence registry
  receipt preparation
  report generation
  runtime adapters

Santo André Laboratory
  first concrete LogLine Lab instance
  research organ / public face / experiment discipline

minilab.work
  frontend and control plane for Santo André Laboratory
  Dan’s infra cockpit
  not semantic source
  not Lab core
  not Foundation

Hermes / runtimes / LABs
  execution body
  admitted workorders only
  evidence return

Supabase/Postgres/projections
  read surfaces and operational projections
  not original authority
```

## Versão final do produto

```txt
minilab.work is the digital pitwall of Santo André Laboratory.

It lets Dan, Translator, Operator, runtimes and evidence lanes face the same operational object.

It does not execute by conversation.
It does not treat UI state as truth.
It does not close receipts from vibes.

It visualizes the Lab, routes work to CLI/labd/Hermes, displays ghosts,
tracks hooks, shows evidence, prepares receipts, and keeps the next safe act visible.
```

Essa é a frase de produto que eu defenderia.

## O corte importante: frontend como “surface”, não “brain”

Eu faria uma seção final chamada **Frontend Law**:

```txt
The frontend may display.
The frontend may request.
The frontend may route.
The frontend may prepare.
The frontend may call CLI/labd APIs.

The frontend may not govern canon.
The frontend may not execute protected consequence.
The frontend may not treat projection as truth.
The frontend may not close receipts.
The frontend may not invent evidence.
The frontend may not erase ghosts.
```

Isso está perfeitamente alinhado ao Vertical Runtime Doctrine: operador, mini-LLM, dispatch, Hermes e LAB não podem impersonar autoridade; evidência não é closure; projeção não é canon; Morning State não é proof. `09_vertical_runtime_doctrine.md`

## Minha recomendação para a versão final

Não transforme essa spec em documento único gigante demais. Ela deveria virar três artefatos:

```txt
01-minilab-work-product-spec.md
  identidade, separação institucional, público/privado, telas, UX, pitwall

02-minilab-work-interface-contract.md
  frontend law, APIs CLI/labd, read models, event stream, auth, boundaries

03-minilab-work-lanes-and-surfaces.md
  Forge, Translator, Operator, Evidence, Receipt Review, hooks, reports, ghost board
```

E um README curto no repo:

```txt
minilab.work
Frontend and operational cockpit for Santo André Laboratory.
```

## O veredito

A spec está certa. O que falta para virar final é:

```txt
1. Trocar “LogLine Lab is the CLI” por “LogLine Lab core is CLI/labd/runtime”.
2. Declarar Forge/Translator/Operator como lanes/offices, não órgãos.
3. Separar Foundation Canon / Lab Practice / Project Canon / Local Overlay.
4. Definir que labd/CLI enforce; frontend displays/routes.
5. Formalizar Daily Lab State como tela inicial.
6. Amarrar Code Lab ao contrato Hermes: code draft ≠ delivery; test output ≠ receipt; workorder ≠ execution; execution report ≠ proof.
```

A forma final, pra mim, é:

```txt
LogLine Lab is the public primitive.
Santo André Laboratory is the first living instance.
minilab.work is its pitwall.
CLI/labd is the operational core.
Hermes is the hand.
LogLine is the wire.
Evidence returns.
Ghosts stay visible.
Receipts close narrowly.
Dan signs consequence.
```

Isso está muito forte.
